{"parentUuid":null,"isSidechain":true,"promptId":"037faac4-a90e-48f6-9041-5732c00f999d","agentId":"a1e546999a1783310","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":"Deep research on worst-case scenario analysis for a crypto trading system. Design for survival, not for profit.\n\nResearch thoroughly:\n\n1. **Enumerate ALL ways the system can lose money**:\n   Category A вҖ” Market risk:\n   - Wrong prediction (model accuracy < 50% for extended period)\n   - Flash crash while positioned (BTC drops 10% in 5 minutes)\n   - Prolonged adverse trend (model trained on different regime)\n   - Liquidation cascade (our position adds to cascade)\n   - Correlation breakdown (cross-market signals stop working)\n\n   Category B вҖ” Execution risk:\n   - Slippage much worse than modeled\n   - Order rejected at critical moment\n   - Double execution (position 2x larger than intended)\n   - Stuck order (can't cancel, can't modify)\n\n   Category C вҖ” Operational risk:\n   - Exchange goes down with open position\n   - API key compromised\n   - Server crash during trading hours\n   - Data feed corruption (bad prices)\n   - Bug in position sizing (10x intended size)\n\n   Category D вҖ” External risk:\n   - Exchange insolvency (all funds lost)\n   - Regulatory action (trading banned)\n   - Stablecoin depeg (USDT/USDC)\n   - Network attack on Bitcoin\n\n2. **For each risk: probability, impact, and mitigation**:\n   Create a full risk matrix with:\n   - Probability: very low (<1%/year), low (1-5%), moderate (5-20%), high (>20%)\n   - Impact: negligible (<1% capital), minor (1-5%), major (5-20%), catastrophic (>20%)\n   - Mitigation: what specific action prevents or reduces impact\n   - Residual risk: what remains after mitigation\n\n3. **The \"what kills you\" hierarchy**:\n   - Level 1 death: total account wipeout (margin call, exchange insolvency)\n   - Level 2 death: >50% drawdown (mathematically recoverable but psychologically not)\n   - Level 3 death: >25% drawdown (triggers halt, months to recover)\n   - Level 4 death: alpha decay (strategy stops working, gradual bleed)\n   For each level: what scenarios cause it, how to prevent it\n\n4. **Worst historical day analysis**:\n   For BTC 5-min data, find:\n   - Worst 5-minute bar (largest single-bar loss)\n   - Worst 30-minute period (6 consecutive bars)\n   - Worst 4-hour period\n   - Worst single day\n   - At our intended position size: what would the loss be in each case?\n\n5. **Reverse stress testing**:\n   - Start from: \"what would cause a 20% drawdown?\"\n   - Work backwards to find the scenarios\n   - For each scenario: how likely is it? How detectable in advance?\n   - This tells you WHERE the real risks are (not where you think they are)\n\n6. **The \"survive everything\" position size**:\n   - Calculate the maximum position size such that:\n     - Worst historical day вҶ’ <5% loss\n     - Worst historical week вҶ’ <10% loss  \n     - Exchange insolvency вҶ’ <20% of net worth (capital allocation limit)\n   - This gives you the MAXIMUM safe position size\n\n7. **Stress test pass/fail criteria**:\n   - Must survive March 2020 COVID crash with <15% DD\n   - Must survive May 2021 China ban with <10% DD\n   - Must survive FTX collapse with <10% DD (operational risk test)\n   - Must survive 48h of zero volatility without >2% cost drag\n   - Must survive 10 consecutive flash crashes in a week\n\n8. **The \"nightmare scenario\" exercise**:\n   - It's 3 AM. You're asleep. BTC drops 15% in 10 minutes.\n   - Your system has a position. Exchange API is slow.\n   - Walk through exactly what happens:\n     - Does the stop loss trigger? (check: exchange-side stop order in place)\n     - Does the kill switch fire? (check: independent monitoring)\n     - What's the maximum possible loss?\n     - Is there a fallback if the primary system is unreachable?\n\n9. **Unknown unknowns**:\n   - What risks HAVEN'T we thought of?\n   - Novel attack vectors in crypto\n   - Regulatory surprises\n   - Technical changes to BTC/exchanges\n   - The role of position sizing as the universal defense\n\n10. **Building the risk budget**:\n    - Start from: \"I can afford to lose $X total before I stop\"\n    - Work backwards:\n      - P(losing $X) < 1% вҶ’ required position size and risk parameters\n      - Verify with Monte Carlo: 10K simulated years\n      - Document: \"at these settings, P(losing 50% of capital) < 0.1%\"\n\nFor each: specific analysis for our system, concrete numbers, action items, and the position sizing implications."},"uuid":"8c77cc4f-2336-4966-8d77-0b5626037e10","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:33:03.940Z","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

    1вҶ’# ep2-crypto: 5-Minute BTC Prediction Engine\n     2вҶ’\n     3вҶ’## Vision\n     4вҶ’A multi-edge Bitcoin price prediction system that combines on-chain signals, order flow microstructure, cross-market lead-lag, and regime-adaptive modeling вҖ” designed to be fundamentally different from the standard LSTM+RSI tutorial approach.\n     5вҶ’\n     6вҶ’---\n     7вҶ’\n     8вҶ’## Phase 0: Documentation Discovery (Completed)\n     9вҶ’\n    10вҶ’### Verified APIs & Libraries\n    11вҶ’\n    12вҶ’**Exchange Data (ccxt pro)**\n    13вҶ’- `watch_order_book(symbol, limit)` вҖ” real-time L2 order book (Binance supports limit=5,10,20,50)\n    14вҶ’- `watch_trades(symbol)` вҖ” aggTrade stream (sub-100ms latency)\n    15вҶ’- `watch_ohlcv(symbol, timeframe)` вҖ” kline streaming\n    16вҶ’- `fetch_open_interest(symbol)` / `fetch_funding_rate(symbol)` вҖ” Bybit derivatives (REST)\n    17вҶ’- Liquidations: NOT in ccxt вҖ” must use Bybit WebSocket directly (`allLiquidation.BTCUSDT`)\n    18вҶ’\n    19вҶ’**On-Chain Data (free, no auth)**\n    20вҶ’- mempool.space: REST + WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`), `track-mempool` for streaming all new txs\n    21вҶ’- Blockchair: SQL-like filtering `?q=output_total(100000000..)` for whale detection (1,440 req/day free)\n    22вҶ’- blockchain.info: `/unconfirmed-transactions`, `/balance`, `/q/*` stats endpoints\n    23вҶ’- Alternative.me: Fear & Greed Index (`GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/`)\n    24вҶ’- Exchange inflow/outflow: NO free API exists вҖ” monitor known exchange addresses as workaround\n    25вҶ’\n    26вҶ’**Cross-Market Data**\n    27вҶ’- ETH: ccxt/Binance WebSocket (free, real-time, sub-100ms) вҖ” clear winner\n    28вҶ’- NQ/Gold/DXY historical: yfinance (`NQ=F`, `GC=F`, `DX-Y.NYB`) вҖ” 5-min bars, 15-min delayed, 60 days depth\n    29вҶ’- NQ/Gold near-real-time polling: Twelve Data (800 req/day free, `XAU/USD`)\n    30вҶ’- DXY: not available as native instrument anywhere free вҖ” must compute from forex components\n    31вҶ’\n    32вҶ’**ML Stack**\n    33вҶ’- XGBoost: `XGBClassifier`, incremental learning via `xgb_model=`, feature importance via `get_score(importance_type='gain')`\n    34вҶ’- PyTorch GRU: `nn.GRU(input_size, hidden_size, num_layers, batch_first=True)`, sequence length 12-60 steps\n    35вҶ’- HMM: `hmmlearn.GaussianHMM(n_components=3)`, no native online learning (use `init_params=\"\"` workaround)\n    36вҶ’- Optuna: `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGB, `trial.report()`+`trial.should_prune()` for PyTorch\n    37вҶ’- Walk-forward: `sklearn.model_selection.TimeSeriesSplit(max_train_size=N)` for sliding window\n    38вҶ’- Feature engineering: `pandas-ta` (or `pandas-ta-classic` as fallback)\n    39вҶ’\n    40вҶ’### Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n    41вҶ’- Never random-split time series data\n    42вҶ’- Never use `bidirectional=True` on GRU (uses future data)\n    43вҶ’- Never run tsfresh in live prediction loop (offline feature discovery only)\n    44вҶ’- Never trust >70% directional accuracy without checking for look-ahead bias\n    45вҶ’- ccxt `binanceusdm` has intermittent WebSocket issues in v4.4.x вҖ” test your version\n    46вҶ’- Bybit order book via ccxt only supports depths [1, 50, 200, 1000] вҖ” slice from 50 for top-10\n    47вҶ’- hmmlearn is in maintenance mode вҖ” plan for potential migration\n    48вҶ’\n    49вҶ’---\n    50вҶ’\n    51вҶ’## Project Structure\n    52вҶ’\n    53вҶ’```\n    54вҶ’ep2-crypto/\n    55вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ pyproject.toml\n    56вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ PLAN.md\n 61вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ db/\n    62вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    63вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ schema.py              # SQLite/TimescaleDB schema\n    64вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ repository.py          # Parameterized query layer\n    65вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest/\n    66вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    67вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ base.py                # Base collector interface\n    68вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ exchange.py            # Binance/Bybit klines, depth, trades\n    69вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ derivatives.py         # OI, funding rate, 72вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ orchestrator.py        # Manages all collectors\n    73вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ features/\n    74вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    75вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ     в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ technical.py           # TA indicators (pandas-ta), volume features\n    80вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ temporal.py            # Cyclical time encoding (sin/cos)\n    81вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ pipeline.py            # Combines all feature sets\n    82вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ regime/\n    83вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    84вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ detector.py            # HMM regime classification\n    85вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ labels.py              # Regime labeling utilities\n    86вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ models/\n    87вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    88вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ xgb_direction.py       # XGBoost direction classifier\n    89вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gru_magnitude.py       # GRU return magnitude predictor\n    90вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ ensemble.py            # Regime-routed ensemble\n    91вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tuning.py              # Optuna hyperparameter optimization\n    92вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ backtest/\n    93вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    94вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ walk_forward.py        # Walk-forward validation engine\n    95вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ metrics.py             # Sharpe, drawdown, profit factor, accuracy\n    96вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ simulator.py           # Execution simulator with slippage/fees\n    97вҶ’в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ api/\n    98вҶ’в”Ӯ           в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n    99вҶ’в”Ӯ           в””в”Җв”Җ server.py              # FastAPI prediction endpoint\n   100вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ scripts/\n   101вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ collect_history.py             # Backfill historical data\n   102вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ train.py                       # Full training pipeline\n   103вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ backtest.py                    # Run backtests\n   104вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ live.py                        # Live prediction loop\n   105вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ tests/\n   106вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_features/\n   107вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_models/\n   108вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_ingest/\n   109вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ test_backtest/\n   110вҶ’в””в”Җв”Җ docker/\n   111вҶ’    в”ңв”Җв”Җ Dockerfile\n   112вҶ’    в””в”Җв”Җ docker-compose.yml\n   113вҶ’```\n   114вҶ’\n   115вҶ’---\n   116вҶ’\n   117вҶ’## Phase 1: Foundation вҖ” Project Setup & Data Storage\n   118вҶ’\n   119вҶ’### What to implement\n   120вҶ’1. Initialize Python project with uv, configure `pyproject.toml` with all dependencies\n   121вҶ’2. Set up SQLite database with schema for: OHLCV candles, order book snapshots, trades, on-chain events, cross-market prices, regime labels\n   122вҶ’3. Build parameterized query repository layer (no string interpolation)\n   123вҶ’4. Set up structlog logging configuration\n   124вҶ’5. Create `config.py` with environment-variable-based settings (no .env files committed)\n   125вҶ’\n   126вҶ’### Dependencies\n   127вҶ’```toml\n   128вҶ’[project]\n   129вҶ’requires-python = \">=3.12\"\n   130вҶ’dependencies = [\n   131вҶ’    \"ccxt>=4.4\",\n   132вҶ’    \"websockets>=13.0\",\n   133вҶ’    \"pandas>=2.2\",\n   134вҶ’    \"numpy>=2.0\",\n   135вҶ’    \"xgboost>=2.1\",\n   136вҶ’    \"torch>=2.5\",\n   137вҶ’    \"hmmlearn>=0.3\",\n   138вҶ’    \"optuna>=4.0\",\n   139вҶ’    \"pandas-ta>=0.3\",\n   140вҶ’    \"scikit-learn>=1.5\",\n   141вҶ’    \"fastapi>=0.115\",\n   142вҶ’    \"uvicorn>=0.32\",\n   143вҶ’    \"structlog>=24.0\",\n   144вҶ’    \"httpx>=0.27\",\n   145вҶ’    \"aiosqlite>=0.20\",\n   146вҶ’]\n   147вҶ’```\n   148вҶ’\n   149вҶ’### Verification\n   150вҶ’- [ ] `uv run python -c \"import ep2_crypto\"` works\n   151вҶ’- [ ] Database creates tables on first run\n   152вҶ’- [ ] All SQL uses parameterized queries (grep for f-strings in db/)\n   153вҶ’- [ ] structlog outputs JSON logs\n   154вҶ’\n   155вҶ’---\n   156вҶ’\n   157вҶ’## Phase 2: Data Ingestion вҖ” Exchange & Derivatives\n   158вҶ’\n   159вҶ’### What to implement\n   160вҶ’1. **Exchange collector** (`ingest/exchange.py`):\n   161вҶ’   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_ohlcv('BTC/USDT:USDT', '1m')` for 1-min klines\n   162вҶ’   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_order_book('BTC/USDT:USDT', limit=20)` for depth snapshots\n   163вҶ’   - ccxt pro WebSocket: `watch_trades('BTC/USDT:USDT')` for aggTrades\n   164вҶ’   - Store each to SQLite at configured intervals\n   165вҶ’\n   166вҶ’2. **Derivatives collector** (`ingest/derivatives.py`):\n   167вҶ’   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_open_interest('BTC/USDT:USDT')` вҖ” poll every 5 min\n   168вҶ’   - ccxt REST: `bybit.fetch_funding_rate('BTC/USDT:USDT')` вҖ” poll every 5 min\n   169вҶ’   - Direct Bybit WebSocket: `allLiquidation.BTCUSDT` stream вҖ” real-time\n   170вҶ’   - Connection: `wss://stream.bybit.com/v5/public/linear`, subscribe `{\"op\":\"subscribe\",\"args\":[\"allLiquidation.BTCUSDT\"]}`\n   171вҶ’\n   172вҶ’3. **Orchestrator** (`ingest/orchestrator.py`):\n   173вҶ’   - Manages all collectors as async tasks\n   174вҶ’   - Handles reconnection, error logging, graceful shutdown\n   175вҶ’   - Health checks for each stream\n   176вҶ’\n   177вҶ’### Documentation references\n   178вҶ’- ccxt pro: `watch_order_book`, `watch_trades`, `watch_ohlcv` вҖ” batch_first pattern\n   179вҶ’- Bybit liquidation: `allLiquidation` topic (NOT deprecated `liquidation` topic)\n   180вҶ’- Bybit WS heartbeat: send `ping` every 20 seconds\n   181вҶ’\n   182вҶ’### Verification\n   183вҶ’- [ ] Run collectors for 10 minutes, verify data in SQLite\n   184вҶ’- [ ] Liquidation events appear when market is volatile\n   185вҶ’- [ ] OI and funding rate update every 5 minutes\n   186вҶ’- [ ] Reconnection works after simulated disconnect\n   187вҶ’- [ ] No duplicate records in database\n   188вҶ’\n   189вҶ’---\n   190вҶ’\n   191вҶ’## Phase 3: Data Ingestion вҖ” On-Chain & Cross-Market\n   192вҶ’\n   193вҶ’### What to implement\n   194вҶ’1. **On-chain collector** (`ingest/onchain.py`):\n   195вҶ’   - mempool.space WebSocket (`wss://mempool.space/api/v1/ws`):\n   196вҶ’     - Subscribe: `{\"action\":\"want\",\"data\":[\"blocks\",\"stats\"]}`\n   197вҶ’     - Subscribe: `{\"track-mempool\": true}` for all new txs\n   198вҶ’     - Client-side filter: flag transactions with output sum > 10 BTC as whale txs\n   199вҶ’   - Blockchair REST (polling every 60s):\n   200вҶ’     - `GET https://api.blockchair.com/bitcoin/mempool/transactions?q=output_total(1000000000..)&s=output_total(desc)`\n   201вҶ’     - Whale transactions > 10 BTC from mempool\n   202вҶ’   - Known exchange address monitoring:\n   203вҶ’     - Maintain a list of top 20 exchange cold/hot wallet addresses\n   204вҶ’     - Poll via mempool.space `/address/:address/txs` every 2 min\n   205вҶ’   - Alternative.me Fear & Greed: `GET https://api.alternative.me/fng/` вҖ” poll every 30 min\n   206вҶ’\n   207вҶ’2. **Cross-market collector** (`ingest/cross_market.py`):\n   208вҶ’   - ETH: ccxt pro `watch_ohlcv('ETH/USDT:USDT', '1m')` вҖ” real-time\n   209вҶ’   - NQ futures: yfinance `yf.download('NQ=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` вҖ” poll every 5 min\n   210вҶ’   - Gold: yfinance `yf.download('GC=F', interval='5m', period='5d')` вҖ” poll every 5 min\n   211вҶ’   - DXY: yfinance `yf.download('DX-Y.NYB', interval='5m', period='5d')` вҖ” poll every 5 min\n   212вҶ’   - Note: yfinance data is ~15 min delayed вҖ” acceptable for lead-lag detection (lag is minutes-to-hours)\n   213вҶ’\n   214вҶ’### Rate limit awareness\n   215вҶ’- Blockchair: max 30 req/min, 1,440/day вҖ” budget carefully\n   216вҶ’- mempool.space: no published limit, be respectful (1 WebSocket connection is fine)\n   217вҶ’- yfinance: no official limit, keep under 100 req/session\n   218вҶ’\n   219вҶ’### Verification\n   220вҶ’- [ ] Whale transactions detected and stored (check against whale-alert Twitter for validation)\n   221вҶ’- [ ] Mempool pressure metrics (size, fee rates) updating in real-time\n   222вҶ’- [ ] ETH price streaming alongside BTC\n   223вҶ’- [ ] NQ/Gold/DXY data updating every 5 min (with 15-min delay noted in metadata)\n   224вҶ’- [ ] Fear & Greed index stored with timestamps\n   225вҶ’\n   226вҶ’---\n   227вҶ’\n   228вҶ’## Phase 4: Feature Engineering вҖ” Microstructure Edge\n   229вҶ’\n   230вҶ’### What to implement\n   231вҶ’1. **Order book features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   232вҶ’   - Bid-ask spread: `(best_ask - best_bid) / mid_price`\n   233вҶ’   - Order book imbalance (top 5 levels): `(bid_vol - ask_vol) / (bid_vol + ask_vol)`\n   234вҶ’   - Depth imbalance: weighted by price proximity to mid\n   235вҶ’   - Book pressure: ratio of volume within 0.1% of mid on each side\n   236вҶ’   - Spread velocity: rate of change of spread over last N snapshots\n   237вҶ’\n   238вҶ’2. **Trade flow features** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   239вҶ’   - Aggressive buy/sell ratio: classify trades by taker side from aggTrade `m` field (buyer is maker = sell aggression)\n   240вҶ’   - Trade intensity: trades per second, rolling 1-min and 5-min\n   241вҶ’   - Volume delta: cumulative (aggressive_buy_vol - aggressive_sell_vol)\n   242вҶ’   - Large trade detection: flag trades > 2 std devs above mean size\n   243вҶ’   - Trade clustering: count of trades in rapid succession (< 100ms apart)\n   244вҶ’\n   245вҶ’3. **Absorption detection** (`features/microstructure.py`):\n   246вҶ’   - Price doesn't move despite large aggressive orders hitting one side\n   247вҶ’   - Measure: large volume delta without proportional price change\n   248вҶ’   - Signal: potential hidden liquidity / institutional activity\n   249вҶ’\n   250вҶ’### Documentation references\n   251вҶ’- Binance aggTrade `m` field: `true` = buyer is market maker (i.e., trade was a sell aggression)\n   252вҶ’- Order book from `watch_order_book`: `ob['bids']` = [[price, amount], ...], `ob['asks']` = [[price, amount], ...]\n   253вҶ’\n   254вҶ’### Verification\n   255вҶ’- [ ] Order book imbalance correlates with short-term price direction (basic sanity check)\n   256вҶ’- [ ] Volume delta calculation matches manual spot-check\n   257вҶ’- [ ] Features update in real-time as new data arrives\n   258вҶ’- [ ] No look-ahead bias in feature calculations (features only use data available at calculation time)\n   259вҶ’\n   260вҶ’---\n   261вҶ’\n   262вҶ’## Phase 5: Feature Engineering вҖ” On-Chain & Cross-Market Edges\n   263вҶ’\n   264вҶ’### What to implement\n   265вҶ’1. **On-chain features** (`features/onchain.py`):\n   266вҶ’   - Whale flow score: net BTC moved to/from exchange addresses in rolling 30-min window\n   267вҶ’   - Mempool pressure: mempool size rate of change, fee spike detection\n   268вҶ’   - Large tx momentum: count and total value of >10 BTC transactions in last 15 min\n   269вҶ’   - Exchange balance delta: change in known exchange address balances (approximation)\n   270вҶ’   - Fear & Greed momentum: rate of change of index (not raw value вҖ” everyone has raw value)\n   271вҶ’\n   272вҶ’2. **Cross-market features** (`features/cross_market.py`):\n   273вҶ’   - Lead-lag correlation: rolling Pearson correlation between BTC returns and NQ/Gold/DXY returns at various lags (0, 1, 2, 5, 10 min)\n   274вҶ’   - Dynamic lead-lag detection: which asset is currently leading? Use Granger causality test on rolling window\n   275вҶ’   - Divergence signals: BTC moving opposite to its current leader = mean reversion signal\n   276вҶ’   - ETH/BTC ratio momentum: rate of change of ETH/BTC price ratio (risk appetite proxy)\n   277вҶ’   - Cross-market volatility spillover: when NQ vol spikes, does BTC vol follow? Rolling correlation of volatility\n   278вҶ’\n   279вҶ’3. **Temporal features** (`features/temporal.py`):\n   280вҶ’   - Cyclical encoding: `sin(2ПҖ Г— minute/60)`, `cos(2ПҖ Г— minute/60)` for minute-of-hour\n   281вҶ’   - Same for hour-of-day, day-of-week\n   282вҶ’   - Session indicator: Asia (00-08 UTC), Europe (08-16 UTC), US (16-00 UTC)\n   283вҶ’   - Time-to-funding: minutes until next Bybit funding rate settlement (every 8h)\n   284вҶ’\n   285вҶ’4. **Technical features** (`features/technical.py`):\n   286вҶ’   - Using pandas-ta: RSI(14), MACD(12,26,9), Bollinger(20,2), ATR(14), VWAP\n   287вҶ’   - Volume: OBV, volume-weighted momentum, volume profile\n   288вҶ’   - Returns: 1m, 5m, 15m, 30m log returns and volatility\n   289вҶ’\n   290вҶ’5. **Feature pipeline** (`features/pipeline.py`):\n   291вҶ’   - Combines all feature sets into single DataFrame\n   292вҶ’   - Handles NaN filling (forward-fill for price, zero for counts)\n   293вҶ’   - Feature normalization (rolling z-score, not global вҖ” prevents look-ahead)\n   294вҶ’   - Outputs: feature matrix aligned to 5-min prediction intervals\n   295вҶ’\n   296вҶ’### Verification\n   297вҶ’- [ ] Lead-lag correlation shows NQ leading BTC during US session (known relationship)\n   298вҶ’- [ ] Whale flow features are non-zero during known large BTC movements\n   299вҶ’- [ ] Feature pipeline produces consistent output shape\n   300вҶ’- [ ] No NaN/Inf values in output\n   301вҶ’- [ ] Rolling z-score uses only past data (no future leakage)\n   302вҶ’\n   303вҶ’---\n   304вҶ’\n   305вҶ’## Phase 6: Regime Detection\n   306вҶ’\n   307вҶ’### What to implement\n   308вҶ’1. **HMM regime detector** (`regime/detector.py`):\n   309вҶ’   - Input features: log returns, realized volatility (12-period rolling std), volume change rate\n   310вҶ’   - Fit `GaussianHMM(n_components=3, covariance_type='full', n_iter=1000)` for 3 regimes\n   311вҶ’   - Label regimes post-hoc by characteristics:\n   312вҶ’     - Trending: high absolute returns, moderate volatility\n   313вҶ’     - Mean-reverting: low returns, low volatility\n   314вҶ’     - Volatile/chaotic: high volatility, mixed returns\n   315вҶ’   - Model selection: fit n=2,3,4,5 and select by BIC\n   316вҶ’   - Pseudo-incremental update: refit every 4 hours on sliding 7-day window with `init_params=\"\"`\n   317вҶ’\n   318вҶ’2. **Regime labels** (`regime/labels.py`):\n   319вҶ’   - Map HMM state indices to semantic labels (states are arbitrary numbers)\n   320вҶ’   - Sort by volatility: lowest vol state = mean-reverting, highest = volatile\n   321вҶ’   - Provide regime probability distribution (not just hard label)\n   322вҶ’   - Regime transition probability: extract from `model.transmat_` for \"regime about to change\" signal\n   323вҶ’\n   324вҶ’### Verification\n   325вҶ’- [ ] 3 distinct regimes visible when plotted against price history\n   326вҶ’- [ ] Regime labels are stable (same market conditions вҶ’ same regime across refits)\n   327вҶ’- [ ] Regime transitions align with known market events (e.g., CPI releases, ETF approvals)\n   328вҶ’- [ ] Regime probabilities sum to 1.0\n   329вҶ’\n   330вҶ’---\n   331вҶ’\n   332вҶ’## Phase 7: Models вҖ” Direction & Magnitude\n   333вҶ’\n   334вҶ’### What to implement\n   335вҶ’1. **XGBoost direction classifier** (`models/xgb_direction.py`):\n   336вҶ’   - Target: 3-class classification (up > +0.1%, down < -0.1%, flat)\n   337вҶ’   - One model per regime (3 regimes Г— 1 XGBoost = 3 models)\n   338вҶ’   - Features: full feature pipeline output\n   339вҶ’   - Training: sliding window walk-forward, retrain every 24h on 14-day window\n   340вҶ’   - Incremental update: `model.fit(X_new, y_new, xgb_model=model.get_booster())`\n   341вҶ’   - Feature importance tracking: log top 20 features per regime per retrain\n   342вҶ’\n   343вҶ’2. **GRU magnitude predictor** (`models/gru_magnitude.py`):\n   344вҶ’   - Target: predicted 5-min return magnitude (regression)\n   345вҶ’   - One model per regime (3 regimes Г— 1 GRU = 3 models)\n   346вҶ’   - Architecture: `GRU(input_size=N, hidden_size=64, num_layers=2, batch_first=True)` вҶ’ `Linear(64, 1)`\n   347вҶ’   - Sequence length: 24 steps (2 hours of 5-min candles) вҖ” tune with Optuna\n   348вҶ’   - Training: sliding window, retrain every 24h, gradient clipping at 1.0\n   349вҶ’   - Never shuffle DataLoader\n   350вҶ’\n   351вҶ’3. **Regime-routed ensemble** (`models/ensemble.py`):\n   352вҶ’   - Input: current regime (from Phase 6), feature matrix\n   353вҶ’   - Route to regime-specific XGBoost + GRU pair\n   354вҶ’   - XGBoost outputs: direction (up/down/flat) + confidence (probability)\n   355вҶ’   - GRU outputs: predicted return magnitude\n   356вҶ’   - Combined signal: `direction Г— magnitude Г— confidence`\n   357вҶ’   - Confidence threshold: only emit signal when XGBoost confidence > 0.6\n   358вҶ’   - Disagreement handling: if XGBoost says up but GRU predicts negative magnitude вҶ’ no signal\n   359вҶ’\n   360вҶ’### Verification\n   361вҶ’- [ ] Each regime-specific model trained on filtered data (only samples from that regime)\n   362вҶ’- [ ] Walk-forward validation shows >52% directional accuracy (above random baseline)\n   363вҶ’- [ ] Feature importance differs meaningfully across regimes\n   364вҶ’- [ ] Ensemble disagreement rate is tracked and logged\n   365вҶ’- [ ] No look-ahead bias: verify test predictions only use training data available before test timestamp\n   366вҶ’\n   367вҶ’---\n   368вҶ’\n   369вҶ’## Phase 8: Hyperparameter Tuning\n   370вҶ’\n   371вҶ’### What to implement\n   372вҶ’1. **Optuna integration** (`models/tuning.py`):\n   373вҶ’   - XGBoost search space:\n   374вҶ’     ```python\n   375вҶ’     max_depth: suggest_int(3, 12)\n   376вҶ’     learning_rate: suggest_float(0.01, 0.3, log=True)\n   377вҶ’     min_child_weight: suggest_int(1, 250)\n   378вҶ’     subsample: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   379вҶ’     colsample_bytree: suggest_float(0.5, 1.0)\n   380вҶ’     reg_lambda: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   381вҶ’     reg_alpha: suggest_float(0.001, 25.0, log=True)\n   382вҶ’     ```\n   383вҶ’   - GRU search space:\n   384вҶ’     ```python\n   385вҶ’     hidden_size: suggest_int(32, 256)\n   386вҶ’     num_layers: suggest_int(1, 3)\n   387вҶ’     lr: suggest_float(1e-5, 1e-2, log=True)\n   388вҶ’     dropout: suggest_float(0.1, 0.5)\n   389вҶ’     seq_len: suggest_int(12, 60)\n   390вҶ’     ```\n   391вҶ’   - HMM: tune `n_components` (2-5) by BIC\n   392вҶ’   - Use `MedianPruner(n_startup_trials=5, n_warmup_steps=10)` for both\n   393вҶ’   - Use `XGBoostPruningCallback` for XGBoost specifically\n   394вҶ’   - Objective: maximize walk-forward Sharpe ratio (not just accuracy)\n   395вҶ’\n   396вҶ’2. **Feature selection via tsfresh** (offline, one-time):\n   397вҶ’   - Run `extract_features` with `EfficientFCParameters` on historical data\n   398вҶ’   - Identify top statistical features (autocorrelation lags, entropy, etc.)\n   399вҶ’   - Implement top 10-15 discovered features manually in the live feature pipeline\n   400вҶ’\n   401вҶ’### Verification\n   402вҶ’- [ ] Optuna study completes 50+ trials per model\n   403вҶ’- [ ] Best hyperparameters improve Sharpe over defaults\n   404вҶ’- [ ] Pruning correctly stops poor trials early\n   405вҶ’- [ ] tsfresh features that made the cut are documented\n   406вҶ’\n   407вҶ’---\n   408вҶ’\n   409вҶ’## Phase 9: Backtesting Framework\n   410вҶ’\n   411вҶ’### What to implement\n   412вҶ’1. **Walk-forward engine** (`backtest/walk_forward.py`):\n   413вҶ’   - Custom implementation (not just sklearn TimeSeriesSplit):\n   414вҶ’     ```python\n   415вҶ’     walk_forward_validate(X, y, model, train_size=4032, test_size=288, step_size=288, gap=1)\n   416вҶ’     # 4032 = 14 days of 5-min candles, 288 = 1 day, gap=1 to prevent leakage\n   417вҶ’     ```\n   418вҶ’   - Sliding window (not expanding) вҖ” crypto regimes shift too fast\n   419вҶ’   - Re-detect regime at each step\n   420вҶ’   - Retrain regime-specific models at each step\n   421вҶ’\n   422вҶ’2. **Execution simulator** (`backtest/simulator.py`):\n   423вҶ’   - Slippage model: 0.01-0.05% per trade (configurable)\n   424вҶ’   - Transaction fees: 0.04% maker / 0.06% taker (Binance futures)\n   425вҶ’   - Latency simulation: 50-200ms delay between signal and execution\n   426вҶ’   - Position sizing: Kelly criterion or fixed fractional\n   427вҶ’   - No trading during regime transitions (confidence < threshold)\n   428вҶ’\n   429вҶ’3. **Metrics** (`backtest/metrics.py`):\n   430вҶ’   - Directional accuracy (per regime)\n   431вҶ’   - Sharpe ratio (annualized)\n   432вҶ’   - Max drawdown\n   433вҶ’   - Profit factor\n   434вҶ’   - Win rate, average win/loss ratio\n   435вҶ’   - Calmar ratio\n   436вҶ’   - Trade count per day\n   437вҶ’   - Regime accuracy (predicted vs actual)\n   438вҶ’\n   439вҶ’### Verification\n   440вҶ’- [ ] Backtest on 30+ days of historical data\n   441вҶ’- [ ] Results include transaction costs (no \"zero-cost\" delusion)\n   442вҶ’- [ ] Sharpe > 0 after costs (basic sanity)\n   443вҶ’- [ ] Compare against baselines: buy-and-hold, momentum, random\n   444вҶ’- [ ] Metrics breakdown per regime shows which regimes are profitable\n   445вҶ’\n   446вҶ’---\n   447вҶ’\n   448вҶ’## Phase 10: API & Live Prediction\n   449вҶ’\n   450вҶ’### What to implement\n   451вҶ’1. **FastAPI server** (`api/server.py`):\n   452вҶ’   - `GET /predict` вҖ” returns current prediction (direction, magnitude, confidence, regime)\n   453вҶ’   - `GET /health` вҖ” checks all data streams are alive, models are loaded, last prediction timestamp\n   454вҶ’   - `GET /metrics` вҖ” live accuracy tracking, rolling Sharpe\n   455вҶ’   - `GET /regime` вҖ” current regime + transition probabilities\n   456вҶ’   - All responses include timestamps and staleness warnings\n   457вҶ’\n   458вҶ’2. **Live prediction loop** (`scripts/live.py`):\n   459вҶ’   - Async event loop running all collectors\n   460вҶ’   - Feature pipeline triggers on each new 5-min candle close\n   461вҶ’   - Regime detection updates\n   462вҶ’   - Model inference вҶ’ prediction\n   463вҶ’   - Store prediction + actual outcome for live accuracy tracking\n   464вҶ’   - Auto-retrain models every 24h on latest data\n   465вҶ’\n   466вҶ’### Verification\n   467вҶ’- [ ] API responds in < 100ms\n   468вҶ’- [ ] Health endpoint actually checks dependencies (not just returns \"ok\")\n   469вҶ’- [ ] Predictions emit within 1 second of candle close\n   470вҶ’- [ ] Live accuracy tracking matches backtest expectations (within reason)\n   471вҶ’- [ ] Graceful degradation: if one data source fails, system still produces predictions (with lower confidence)\n   472вҶ’\n   473вҶ’---\n   474вҶ’\n   475вҶ’## Phase 11: Historical Backfill & Full Validation\n   476вҶ’\n   477вҶ’### What to implement\n   478вҶ’1. **Historical data collection** (`scripts/collect_history.py`):\n   479вҶ’   - Binance REST: fetch 30-60 days of 1-min OHLCV via `exchange.fetch_ohlcv()`\n   480вҶ’   - Bybit REST: backfill OI history (`fetch_open_interest_history`) and funding rate history\n   481вҶ’   - yfinance: backfill NQ, Gold, DXY 5-min data (limited to 60 days)\n   482вҶ’   - Note: order book and trade-level data cannot be backfilled вҖ” microstructure features start from collection date\n   483вҶ’\n   484вҶ’2. **Full system validation**:\n   485вҶ’   - Run complete pipeline: ingest вҶ’ features вҶ’ regime вҶ’ models вҶ’ backtest\n   486вҶ’   - Compare regime detection against known market events\n   487вҶ’   - Validate that each edge contributes independently (ablation study):\n   488вҶ’     - Model with all features vs model without microstructure\n   489вҶ’     - Model with all features vs model without on-chain\n   490вҶ’     - Model with all features vs model without cross-market\n   491вҶ’     - Model with all features vs model without regime routing\n   492вҶ’\n   493вҶ’### Verification\n   494вҶ’- [ ] Each edge shows positive marginal contribution in ablation study\n   495вҶ’- [ ] Full system Sharpe > any single-edge system\n   496вҶ’- [ ] No edge has negative contribution (remove if so)\n   497вҶ’- [ ] System handles missing data gracefully (e.g., no on-chain data for first 30 days)\n   498вҶ’\n   499вҶ’---\n   500вҶ’\n   501вҶ’## Execution Order & Dependencies\n   502вҶ’\n   503вҶ’```\n   504вҶ’Phase 1 (Foundation)\n   505вҶ’  вҶ“\n   506вҶ’Phase 2 (Exchange Ingestion) в”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”Җв”җ\n   507вҶ’  вҶ“                                 в”Ӯ\n   508вҶ’Phase 3 (On-Chain + Cross-Market) в”Җв”Ө\n   509вҶ’  вҶ“                                 в”Ӯ\n   510вҶ’Phase 4 (Microstructure Features) в”Җв”Җв”Өв”Җв”Җ can partially parallelize\n   511вҶ’  вҶ“                                 в”Ӯ\n   512вҶ’Phase 5 (On-Chain + Cross Features)в”ҳ\n   513вҶ’  вҶ“\n   514вҶ’Phase 6 (Regime Detection)\n   515вҶ’  вҶ“\n   516вҶ’Phase 7 (Models)\n   517вҶ’  вҶ“\n   518вҶ’Phase 8 (Tuning)\n   519вҶ’  вҶ“\n   520вҶ’Phase 9 (Backtesting)\n   521вҶ’  вҶ“\n   522вҶ’Phase 10 (API + Live)\n   523вҶ’  вҶ“\n   524вҶ’Phase 11 (Validation + Ablation)\n   525вҶ’```\n   526вҶ’\n   527вҶ’Phases 2-5 can overlap: start collecting data in Phase 2-3 while building features in Phase 4-5. Models (Phase 7) need data from all feature phases.\n   528вҶ’\n   529вҶ’---\n   530вҶ’\n   531вҶ’## Key Design Decisions\n   532вҶ’\n   533вҶ’1. **Sliding window, not expanding** вҖ” crypto non-stationarity means old data hurts more than helps\n   534вҶ’2. **Per-regime models** вҖ” a trending market model is useless in a ranging market\n   535вҶ’3. **Confidence gating** вҖ” no signal is better than a low-confidence signal\n   536вҶ’4. **Magnitude + direction separation** вҖ” XGBoost excels at classification, GRU at regression\n   537вҶ’5. **15-min delay on cross-market is acceptable** вҖ” the lead-lag relationship operates on minutes-to-hours, not seconds\n   538вҶ’6. **No exchange flow data** вҖ” no free API exists; we approximate via address monitoring\n   539вҶ’7. **SQLite for dev** вҖ” zero setup, switch to TimescaleDB when moving to production\n   540вҶ’8. **Feature normalization via rolling z-score** вҖ” prevents global normalization look-ahead bias\n   541вҶ’"}]},"uuid":"7fe81070-a9d2-404e-b358-3ec6bd49ffe8","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:33:20.582Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"8132fe8a-7922-4ea6-9b16-bfbcda17c74b","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

{"parentUuid":"e6cf468c-bde8-47fa-8aa4-dae234c4c346","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"037faac4-a90e-48f6-9041-5732c00f999d","agentId":"a1e546999a1783310","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01QwGZiAL3jFtabQcGLGCwyX","type":"tool_result","content":"     1вҶ’# Architecture Decision Records (ADRs)\n     2вҶ’\n     3вҶ’## ADR-001: LightGBM over XGBoost\n     4вҶ’\n     5вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n     6вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n     7вҶ’\n     8вҶ’### Context\n     9вҶ’The original plan specified XGBoost as the primary classifier. Research across multiple reports consistently showed LightGBM outperforms XGBoost on 5-min crypto prediction tasks.\n    10вҶ’\n    11вҶ’### Decision\n    12вҶ’Use LightGBM as the primary gradient boosting classifier.\n    13вҶ’\n    14вҶ’### Consequences\n    15вҶ’- **Positive**: 0.5-1.5% accuracy improvement on 5-min crypto data\n    16вҶ’- **Positive**: Faster training (leaf-wise growth vs level-wise)\n    17вҶ’- **Positive**: Native categorical feature support\n    18вҶ’- **Positive**: Lower memory footprint\n    19вҶ’- **Negative**: Slightly different API from XGBoost (minor migration effort)\n    20вҶ’- **Negative**: Can overfit more easily with small data (mitigated by `min_child_samples=50`)\n    21вҶ’\n    22вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n    23вҶ’- **XGBoost**: Slower, slightly lower accuracy on this specific task. Well-documented but no advantage here.\n    24вҶ’- **TabNet**: Self-attention mechanism promising but inconsistent results, harder to tune, 2-3x slower inference.\n    25вҶ’- **Random Forest**: Baseline model, consistently outperformed by boosting.\n    26вҶ’\n    27вҶ’### Research Source\n    28вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section \"Core Model: LightGBM + Stacking Ensemble\"\n    29вҶ’- Multiple research files confirming LightGBM > XGBoost on crypto tick data\n    30вҶ’\n    31вҶ’---\n    32вҶ’\n    33вҶ’## ADR-002: Ternary Target over Binary\n    34вҶ’\n    35вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    36вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n    37вҶ’\n    38вҶ’### Context\n    39вҶ’The original plan used binary classification (up/down). Research showed this forces the model to make predictions during low-volatility periods where no tradeable edge exists.\n    40вҶ’\n    41вҶ’### Decision\n    42вҶ’Use ternary classification: UP (return > +threshold), DOWN (return < -threshold), FLAT (within threshold). The threshold is adaptive per regime.\n    43вҶ’\n    44вҶ’### Consequences\n    45вҶ’- **Positive**: Acknowledges untradeable low-volatility periods\n    46вҶ’- **Positive**: Reduces false signals during quiet markets\n    47вҶ’- **Positive**: Adaptive threshold adjusts to current market conditions\n    48вҶ’- **Negative**: Three-class problem is harder than binary\n    49вҶ’- **Negative**: Class imbalance (FLAT may dominate in low-vol regimes)\n    50вҶ’- **Negative**: Threshold selection adds a hyperparameter\n    51вҶ’\n    52вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n    53вҶ’- **Binary (up/down)**: Simpler but forces predictions during untradeable periods\n    54вҶ’- **Regression (continuous returns)**: Harder to calibrate, confidence gating less natural\n    55вҶ’- **Binary + volatility filter**: Two-step approach, less elegant than integrated ternary\n    56вҶ’\n    57вҶ’### Research Source\n    58вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section \"Revised Tech Stack\" (Target row)\n    59вҶ’- Research on Lopez de Prado's triple barrier method\n    60вҶ’\n    61вҶ’---\n    62вҶ’\n    63вҶ’## ADR-003: Sliding Window over Expanding Window\n    64вҶ’\n    65вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    66вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n    67вҶ’\n    68вҶ’### Context\n    69вҶ’Standard walk-forward validation uses expanding windows (all historical data). Crypto markets exhibit strong non-stationarity where patterns from months ago may be counterproductive.\n    70вҶ’\n    71вҶ’### Decision\n    72вҶ’Use 14-day sliding windows for training. Old data is dropped, not accumulated.\n    73вҶ’\n    74вҶ’### Consequences\n    75вҶ’- **Positive**: Model adapts to current market regime faster\n    76вҶ’- **Positive**: Training time stays constant (not growing)\n    77вҶ’- **Positive**: Reduces impact of regime changes from distant past\n    78вҶ’- **Negative**: Less training data per fold (4,032 bars vs potentially 100K+)\n    79вҶ’- **Negative**: May miss rare but important patterns (e.g., flash crash behavior)\n    80вҶ’\n    81вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n    82вҶ’- **Expanding window**: Standard approach, but crypto non-stationarity means old data hurts\n    83вҶ’- **Weighted expanding**: Decay weight on old samples. More complex, marginal benefit over sliding\n    84вҶ’- **21-day window**: Research showed >21 days dilutes signal in crypto\n    85вҶ’- **7-day window**: Too little data, model underfits\n    86вҶ’\n    87вҶ’### Research Source\n    88вҶ’- `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` section \"Walk-Forward Validation Protocol\"\n    89вҶ’- Research consensus: \"Recency premium in crypto; >21 days dilutes signal\"\n    90вҶ’\n    91вҶ’---\n    92вҶ’\n    93вҶ’## ADR-004: On-Chain as Regime Context Only\n    94вҶ’\n    95вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n    96вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n    97вҶ’\n    98вҶ’### Context\n    99вҶ’The original plan used on-chain data (whale flows, mempool, exchange balances) as primary prediction signals. Research revealed these signals operate at 4h-24h timescales, not 5-min.\n   100вҶ’\n   101вҶ’### Decision\n   102вҶ’Downgrade on-chain data to regime context only. Use mempool whale detection (>10 BTC to known exchange addresses) as a background signal, not for direct 5-min prediction.\n   103вҶ’\n   104вҶ’### Consequences\n   105вҶ’- **Positive**: Removes noise from feature set at 5-min timescale\n   106вҶ’- **Positive**: Reduces data source dependencies (fewer failure points)\n   107вҶ’- **Positive**: Simpler pipeline\n   108вҶ’- **Negative**: Loses potential long-horizon signals (acceptable for 5-min system)\n   109вҶ’- **Negative**: May miss large exchange inflow/outflow signals\n   110вҶ’\n   111вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   112вҶ’- **On-chain as primary signal**: Research shows these are 4h+ signals, not 5-min\n   113вҶ’- **Skip on-chain entirely**: Loses useful regime context (e.g., whale activity as volatility predictor)\n   114вҶ’- **Multi-horizon model**: Could use on-chain at 4h and microstructure at 5-min, but adds massive complexity\n   115вҶ’\n   116вҶ’### Research Source\n   117вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"On-chain signals operate at 4h-24h, NOT 5-min\"\n   118вҶ’- Research files on whale detection and exchange flows\n   119вҶ’\n   120вҶ’---\n   121вҶ’\n   122вҶ’## ADR-005: Skip Real-Time Sentiment, Use Funding Rate\n   123вҶ’\n   124вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   125вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   126вҶ’\n   127вҶ’### Context\n   128вҶ’The original plan included Twitter/social sentiment NLP analysis. Research showed that by the time sentiment signals are processed and available, the price has already moved at the 5-min timescale.\n   129вҶ’\n   130вҶ’### Decision\n   131вҶ’Skip all NLP-based sentiment analysis. Use Bybit funding rate as the only \"sentiment\" proxy, as it is quantitative, real-time, and directly actionable.\n   132вҶ’\n   133вҶ’### Consequences\n   134вҶ’- **Positive**: Eliminates slow, noisy, and expensive NLP pipeline\n   135вҶ’- **Positive**: Funding rate is free, real-time, and quantitative\n   136вҶ’- **Positive**: Reduces infrastructure complexity significantly\n   137вҶ’- **Negative**: Misses potential early signals from viral social media events\n   138вҶ’- **Negative**: Funding rate is lagging indicator of sentiment, not leading\n   139вҶ’\n   140вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   141вҶ’- **Twitter NLP (FinBERT/GPT)**: Too slow for 5-min (30-60s processing time)\n   142вҶ’- **Fear & Greed Index**: Daily resolution, useless for 5-min. Kept as regime context only.\n   143вҶ’- **News API sentiment**: Same latency problem as social media\n   144вҶ’- **Telegram/Discord scraping**: Legal concerns, unreliable, high noise\n   145вҶ’\n   146вҶ’### Research Source\n   147вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"Sentiment analysis вҶ’ skip for 5-min вҖ” too slow\"\n   148вҶ’- Research files on sentiment analysis latency\n   149вҶ’\n   150вҶ’---\n   151вҶ’\n   152вҶ’## ADR-006: Stacking Ensemble over Per-Regime Models\n   153вҶ’\n   154вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   155вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   156вҶ’\n   157вҶ’### Context\n   158вҶ’The original plan trained separate model sets per regime (3 regimes x 2 models = 6 models). Research showed this fragments already-scarce data, leading to undertrained models.\n   159вҶ’\n   160вҶ’### Decision\n   161вҶ’Use a single stacking ensemble (LightGBM + CatBoost + GRU) with regime as an input feature, not a routing mechanism. Stacking meta-learner (logistic regression) combines base model predictions.\n   162вҶ’\n   163вҶ’### Consequences\n   164вҶ’- **Positive**: All training data available to all models (no fragmentation)\n   165вҶ’- **Positive**: Stacking is the #1 ensemble gain after feature engineering (Kaggle consensus)\n   166вҶ’- **Positive**: 2-5% improvement over best single model\n   167вҶ’- **Positive**: Models learn regime-dependent patterns via regime input features\n   168вҶ’- **Negative**: Single model set may be less specialized per regime\n   169вҶ’- **Negative**: Stacking adds complexity (OOF predictions required)\n   170вҶ’\n   171вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   172вҶ’- **Per-regime models**: Fragments data (e.g., volatile regime may have only 15% of samples)\n   173вҶ’- **Simple averaging**: Worse than stacking, no learned combination weights\n   174вҶ’- **Bayesian Model Averaging**: Theoretically superior but harder to implement, marginal gain\n   175вҶ’- **Mixture of Experts**: More complex, similar to per-regime but with soft routing. Future consideration.\n   176вҶ’\n   177вҶ’### Research Source\n   178вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md`: \"Per-regime models fragment already-scarce data\"\n   179вҶ’- Kaggle consensus on stacking as top ensemble method\n   180вҶ’\n   181вҶ’---\n   182вҶ’\n   183вҶ’## ADR-007: Meta-Labeling for Confidence Gating\n   184вҶ’\n   185вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   186вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   187вҶ’\n   188вҶ’### Context\n   189вҶ’A raw ML prediction with 53% accuracy is not profitable after transaction costs. We need a way to select only the highest-conviction trades. Lopez de Prado's meta-labeling technique trains a secondary model to predict whether a primary model's trade will be profitable.\n   190вҶ’\n   191вҶ’### Decision\n   192вҶ’Implement meta-labeling as a core gate in the confidence pipeline. A secondary LightGBM model takes the primary prediction + features + regime and outputs probability of profitable trade.\n   193вҶ’\n   194вҶ’### Consequences\n   195вҶ’- **Positive**: 50-100% Sharpe improvement (research consensus)\n   196вҶ’- **Positive**: Dramatically reduces trade count (fewer but better trades)\n   197вҶ’- **Positive**: Naturally adapts to changing market conditions\n   198вҶ’- **Positive**: Provides interpretable confidence score\n   199вҶ’- **Negative**: Requires careful implementation to avoid data leakage\n   200вҶ’- **Negative**: Reduces number of trades (may miss some profitable opportunities)\n   201вҶ’- **Negative**: Two-model system is harder to debug\n   202вҶ’\n   203вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   204вҶ’- **Fixed confidence threshold**: Simple but not adaptive\n   205вҶ’- **Ensemble agreement only**: Weaker signal than meta-labeling\n   206вҶ’- **Manual signal filters**: Not learnable, requires constant tuning\n   207вҶ’- **No gating**: 53% accuracy is unprofitable after costs\n   208вҶ’\n   209вҶ’### Research Source\n   210вҶ’- `research/meta_labeling_deep_research.md` - Full implementation guide\n   211вҶ’- Lopez de Prado, \"Advances in Financial Machine Learning\" (AFML)\n   212вҶ’\n   213вҶ’---\n   214вҶ’\n   215вҶ’## ADR-008: Triple Barrier Labeling over Fixed Threshold\n   216вҶ’\n   217вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   218вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   219вҶ’\n   220вҶ’### Context\n   221вҶ’Simple fixed-threshold labeling (if return > X bps, label \"up\") ignores the path of the price. A trade that hits a stop loss before eventually being correct should not be labeled as a win.\n   222вҶ’\n   223вҶ’### Decision\n   224вҶ’Use triple barrier labeling (Lopez de Prado): vertical barrier (time limit), upper barrier (take profit), lower barrier (stop loss). The label is determined by which barrier is touched first.\n   225вҶ’\n   226вҶ’### Consequences\n   227вҶ’- **Positive**: More realistic labels that account for path dependency\n   228вҶ’- **Positive**: Naturally handles holding period (vertical barrier)\n   229вҶ’- **Positive**: Stop loss incorporated into label definition\n   230вҶ’- **Positive**: Better alignment between backtest labels and live trading outcomes\n   231вҶ’- **Negative**: More complex to implement than fixed threshold\n   232вҶ’- **Negative**: Labels depend on barrier parameters (additional hyperparameters)\n   233вҶ’- **Negative**: Computing labels is slower (must simulate forward from each point)\n   234вҶ’\n   235вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   236вҶ’- **Fixed threshold**: Simple but ignores path. A trade that drops 2% before recovering is labeled \"win\"\n   237вҶ’- **Forward return only**: Standard in academia but doesn't match trading reality\n   238вҶ’- **Realized P&L labeling**: Requires a trading strategy to exist before labeling, circular\n   239вҶ’\n   240вҶ’### Research Source\n   241вҶ’- Lopez de Prado, \"Advances in Financial Machine Learning\" Chapter 3\n   242вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` references to AFML techniques\n   243вҶ’\n   244вҶ’---\n   245вҶ’\n   246вҶ’## ADR-009: Event-Driven Backtest Engine with Numba\n   247вҶ’\n   248вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   249вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   250вҶ’\n   251вҶ’### Context\n   252вҶ’Vectorized backtesting is fast but cannot model path-dependent behavior (partial fills, stop losses, latency). Pure Python event-driven backtesting is realistic but 100x too slow for large-scale walk-forward validation.\n   253вҶ’\n   254вҶ’### Decision\n   255вҶ’Build a custom event-driven backtest engine with Numba-compiled inner loop. Use vectorized backtesting for initial signal research (fast iteration), event-driven for final validation (realistic fills).\n   256вҶ’\n   257вҶ’### Consequences\n   258вҶ’- **Positive**: 100x speedup over pure Python event-driven\n   259вҶ’- **Positive**: Realistic execution modeling (slippage, partial fills, latency)\n   260вҶ’- **Positive**: Path-dependent behavior correctly modeled\n   261вҶ’- **Positive**: < 3 seconds per year of 5-min bars (fast enough for walk-forward)\n   262вҶ’- **Negative**: Numba compilation adds startup time\n   263вҶ’- **Negative**: Numba code is harder to debug (limited Python features)\n   264вҶ’- **Negative**: Requires careful data type management (Numba type restrictions)\n   265вҶ’\n   266вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   267вҶ’- **Pure vectorized (numpy)**: Fast (0.1s/year) but cannot model execution realistically\n   268вҶ’- **Pure Python event-driven**: Realistic but ~300s/year (too slow for walk-forward)\n   269вҶ’- **Existing frameworks (Backtrader, Zipline)**: Not designed for 5-min crypto, limited customization\n   270вҶ’- **C++ engine**: Maximum performance but high development cost, harder to iterate\n   271вҶ’\n   272вҶ’### Research Source\n   273вҶ’- `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` section \"Engine: Custom Event-Driven + Vectorized Hybrid\"\n   274вҶ’\n   275вҶ’---\n   276вҶ’\n   277вҶ’## ADR-010: asyncio Single-Process Architecture\n   278вҶ’\n   279вҶ’**Date**: 2026-03-23\n   280вҶ’**Status**: Accepted\n   281вҶ’\n   282вҶ’### Context\n   283вҶ’The system must manage multiple WebSocket connections, REST polling, feature computation, model inference, and API serving concurrently. Options are multiprocessing, threading, or asyncio.\n   284вҶ’\n   285вҶ’### Decision\n   286вҶ’Use asyncio in a single process for all concurrent operations. Model training (CPU-intensive) is the only operation that may optionally use a separate process.\n   287вҶ’\n   288вҶ’### Consequences\n   289вҶ’- **Positive**: No inter-process communication overhead\n   290вҶ’- **Positive**: Simple shared state (no serialization needed)\n   291вҶ’- **Positive**: Lower memory footprint than multiprocessing\n   292вҶ’- **Positive**: Natural fit for I/O-bound workloads (WebSocket, REST polling)\n   293вҶ’- **Positive**: ccxt pro is natively async\n   294вҶ’- **Negative**: CPU-bound operations block the event loop (mitigated by running in executor)\n   295вҶ’- **Negative**: Single point of failure (one crash kills everything)\n   296вҶ’- **Negative**: Cannot utilize multiple CPU cores for parallel computation\n   297вҶ’\n   298вҶ’### Alternatives Considered\n   299вҶ’- **Multiprocessing**: Better CPU utilization but complex IPC, higher memory, harder to share state\n   300вҶ’- **Threading**: GIL limits CPU parallelism, harder to reason about concurrency\n   301вҶ’- **Actor model (Ray)**: Overkill for this scale, adds infrastructure dependency\n   302вҶ’- **Microservices**: Each component as separate service. Too much overhead for single-developer project\n   303вҶ’\n   304вҶ’### Research Source\n   305вҶ’- `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` section on system architecture\n   306вҶ’- Research files on production system design\n   307вҶ’"}]},"uuid":"daccbe14-74ab-48e2-b07d-0899f91e7928","timestamp":"2026-03-23T13:33:21.447Z","sourceToolAssistantUUID":"e6cf468c-bde8-47fa-8aa4-dae234c4c346","userType":"external","entrypoint":"claude-vscode","cwd":"/Users/edgarpocaterra/ep2-crypto","sessionId":"f48c9af0-2e30-4c92-9024-4c84a03f39db","version":"2.1.81","gitBranch":"main","slug":"spicy-gathering-plum"}

{"parentUuid":"c648eb48-8684-4b0a-8301-a4f036d30c17","isSidechain":true,"promptId":"037faac4-a90e-48f6-9041-5732c00f999d","agentId":"a1e546999a1783310","type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01XgYwWVCgN2P3QdeB5dwKSU","type":"tool_result","content":"     1вҶ’# ep2-crypto: 5-Minute BTC Prediction Engine\n     2вҶ’\n     3вҶ’## Project Overview\n     4вҶ’\n     5вҶ’ep2-crypto is a multi-edge Bitcoin price prediction system targeting 5-minute directional forecasts on BTC/USDT perpetual futures. It combines order flow microstructure, cross-market lead-lag, regime-adaptive modeling, and confidence gating to achieve a tradeable edge.\n     6вҶ’\n     7вҶ’**Realistic expectations** (from 500K+ words of research):\n     8вҶ’- Directional accuracy: 52-56% at 5-min horizon\n     9вҶ’- Backtest-to-live Sharpe degradation: 50-70% (need Sharpe >2.0 in backtest to survive)\n    10вҶ’- Round-trip costs: 8-12 bps minimum\n    11вҶ’- Alpha half-life: 1-6 months for ML patterns\n    12вҶ’- Optimal feature count: 18-25 (not 200+)\n    13вҶ’\n    14вҶ’## Tech Stack\n    15вҶ’\n    16вҶ’| Component | Choice | Why |\n    17вҶ’|-----------|--------|-----|\n    18вҶ’| Language | Python 3.12+ | ML ecosystem, async support |\n    19вҶ’| Package manager | uv | Fast, deterministic (never pip/poetry) |\n    20вҶ’| Primary model | LightGBM | Outperforms XGBoost by 0.5-1.5% on 5-min crypto |\n    21вҶ’| Secondary model | CatBoost | Ordered boosting prevents leakage, adds diversity |\n    22вҶ’| Sequence model | GRU (PyTorch) | Hidden state extracted as features for LightGBM |\n    23вҶ’| Ensemble | Stacking (logistic regression meta-learner) | 2-5% over best single model |\n    24вҶ’| Regime detection | Hierarchical (HMM + BOCPD + GARCH + Efficiency Ratio) | Faster detection than HMM alone |\n    25вҶ’| Exchange data | ccxt (WebSocket + REST) | Binance WS for klines/depth/trades, Bybit for derivatives |\n    26вҶ’| Cross-market | yfinance, Twelve Data | NQ, Gold, DXY (15-min delayed, acceptable) |\n    27вҶ’| On-chain | mempool.space WS | Whale detection only (on-chain operates at 4h+, not 5-min) |\n    28вҶ’| Logging | structlog | Structured JSON logs, never print() |\n    29вҶ’| API | FastAPI + uvicorn | Prediction endpoints, health, metrics |\n    30вҶ’| Database | SQLite (dev) -> TimescaleDB (prod) | Zero setup for dev |\n    31вҶ’| Inference | ONNX Runtime | 2-5x speedup over native |\n    32вҶ’| Tuning | Optuna | MedianPruner, Sharpe objective |\n    33вҶ’| Testing | pytest + pytest-cov | Required for every feature computation |\n    34вҶ’| Linting | ruff + mypy (strict) | Type safety, code quality |\n    35вҶ’\n    36вҶ’## Key Architecture Decisions\n    37вҶ’\n    38вҶ’These decisions are the result of extensive research (49 files in `research/`). Do NOT change them without reviewing the corresponding ADR in `DECISIONS.md`.\n    39вҶ’\n    40вҶ’### Model Architecture\n    41вҶ’- **LightGBM over XGBoost** (ADR-001): Faster training, better accuracy on crypto tick data\n    42вҶ’- **Stacking ensemble over per-regime models** (ADR-006): Per-regime models fragment scarce data. Single ensemble with regime as input feature is more robust\n    43вҶ’- **Ternary target (up/flat/down) with adaptive threshold** (ADR-002): Acknowledges untradeable low-volatility periods. Threshold adapts per regime\n    44вҶ’- **Triple barrier labeling over fixed threshold** (ADR-008): Accounts for time decay and stop-loss, produces more realistic labels\n    45вҶ’\n    46вҶ’### Data & Features\n    47вҶ’- **Dual normalization pipeline** (ADR in RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md): Raw features for tree models (normalization harms trees), robust scaling + rank-to-gaussian for neural models\n    48вҶ’- **On-chain as regime context only, not primary signal** (ADR-004): On-chain signals operate at 4h-24h, not 5-min\n    49вҶ’- **Skip real-time sentiment, use funding rate** (ADR-005): NLP sentiment too slow for 5-min. Funding rate is the only useful \"sentiment\" at this timeframe\n    50вҶ’- **Feature priority**: Microstructure (OBI, OFI, microprice) captures 60-80% of achievable 5-min signal\n    51вҶ’\n    52вҶ’### Validation & Risk\n    53вҶ’- **Purged walk-forward validation**: 14-day sliding window, 18-bar purge (90 min), 12-bar embargo (60 min). Sliding, NOT expanding (crypto non-stationarity)\n    54вҶ’- **Confidence gating pipeline**: isotonic calibration -> meta-labeling -> conformal prediction -> adaptive threshold -> drawdown gate. This is the single biggest Sharpe multiplier (2-4x)\n    55вҶ’- **Quarter-Kelly position sizing**: Position size = 0.25 * Kelly fraction * confidence score\n    56вҶ’- **Annualization**: sqrt(105,120) for 24/7 crypto. 288 bars/day * 365 days = 105,120 bars/year. NEVER use sqrt(252)\n    57вҶ’\n    58вҶ’### Infrastructure\n    59вҶ’- **asyncio single-process architecture** (ADR-010): All collectors and processing in one event loop\n    60вҶ’- **Event-driven backtest engine with Numba** (ADR-009): 100x faster than pure Python, realistic fills\n    61вҶ’- **Numpy ring buffers** for data structures: 10-20x less memory than pandas DataFrames on hot path\n    62вҶ’\n    63вҶ’## Code Conventions\n    64вҶ’\n    65вҶ’### Mandatory Rules\n    66вҶ’1. **Named exports only** - never use `export default` or bare module-level assignments\n    67вҶ’2. **structlog for all logging** - never use `print()` for any output\n    68вҶ’3. **Parameterized SQL queries only** - never use f-strings or string interpolation for SQL\n    69вҶ’4. **All features must use only past data** - no look-ahead bias. Every feature computation at time t may only use data from times <= t\n    70вҶ’5. **Type hints on all functions** - mypy strict mode is enforced\n    71вҶ’6. **Tests required for every feature computation** - including golden dataset tests against hand-verified values\n    72вҶ’7. **No `any` types** - be explicit with all type annotations\n    73вҶ’8. **No TODO/FIXME/HACK without linked issue** - if you must leave one, create a GitHub issue first\n    74вҶ’9. **Secrets via environment variables** - never commit API keys, never use .env files in repo\n    75вҶ’\n    76вҶ’### Error Handling\n    77вҶ’- Always use try/catch with meaningful error messages at system boundaries\n    78вҶ’- Never swallow errors silently - log with context via structlog\n    79вҶ’- Never fire-and-forget async operations - track completion\n    80вҶ’- Health endpoints must check actual dependencies, not just return \"ok\"\n    81вҶ’\n    82вҶ’### Feature Engineering Rules\n    83вҶ’- Every feature must be tested for look-ahead bias (shuffle test + truncation test)\n    84вҶ’- Rolling calculations use only past data (no centered windows)\n    85вҶ’- NaN handling: forward-fill for price data, zero for counts, drop for model input\n    86вҶ’- All normalization fitted on training data only, per fold\n    87вҶ’\n    88вҶ’### Commit Hygiene\n    89вҶ’- Meaningful commit messages explaining WHY, not just WHAT\n    90вҶ’- Pass lint + typecheck + test before committing\n    91вҶ’- One logical change per commit, max 5 commits per feature\n    92вҶ’- Build one feature, verify, commit - never batch 5 features\n    93вҶ’\n    94вҶ’## Project Structure\n    95вҶ’\n    96вҶ’```\n    97вҶ’ep2-crypto/\n    98вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ CLAUDE.md                    # THIS FILE - project context for AI sessions\n    99вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ PLAN.md                      # Original development plan (Phase 0-11)\n   100вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md        # Distilled findings from 49 research files\n   101вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ BACKTESTING_PLAN.md          # Comprehensive backtesting methodology\n   102вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ SPRINTS.md                   # Sprint planning with acceptance criteria\n   103вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ REQUIREMENTS.md              # Functional and non-functional requirements\n   104вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ DECISIONS.md                 # Architecture Decision Records (ADR-001 to ADR-010)\n   105вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ pyproject.toml               # Dependencies and tool configuration\n   106вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ uv.lock                      # Locked dependencies\n   107вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ research/                    # 49 research files (read-only reference)\n   108вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ meta_labeling_deep_research.md\n   109вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ microstructure_ofi_microprice.md\n   110вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ monte_carlo_validation.md\n   111вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ retraining_strategies.md\n   112вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ statistical_validation_tests.py\n   113вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ STRESS_TESTING.md\n   114вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ transaction_cost_modeling.md\n   115вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ... (42 more research files)\n   116вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ src/\n   117вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ ep2_crypto/\n   118вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n   119вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ config.py                  # Pydantic Settings, env-var based\n   120вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ db/\n   121вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ schema.py              # SQLite/TimescaleDB schema\n   122вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ repository.py          # Parameterized query layer\n   123вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ ingest/\n   124вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ base.py                # Base collector interface\n   125вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ exchange.py            # Binance WS: klines, depth@100ms, aggTrades\n   126вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ derivatives.py         # Bybit: OI, funding, liquidations\n   127вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ onchain.py             # mempool.space: whale detection\n   128вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cross_market.py        # NQ, Gold, DXY, ETH\n   129вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ macro.py               # Economic calendar, event monitoring\n   130вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ orchestrator.py        # Async task management, reconnection\n   131вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ features/\n   132вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ base.py                # Feature pipeline interface\n   133вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ microstructure.py      # OBI, OFI, microprice, spread, TFI\n   134вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ volume.py              # Volume delta, VWAP deviation, rate-of-change\n   135вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ volatility.py          # Realized, Parkinson, EWMA, vol-of-vol\n   136вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ momentum.py            # ROC, RSI, linreg slope, quantile rank\n   137вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cross_market.py        # Lead-lag, correlation, divergence\n   138вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ temporal.py            # Cyclical encoding, session, time-to-funding\n   139вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ regime_features.py     # ER, GARCH vol, HMM probs as features\n   140вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ normalization.py       # Dual pipeline (raw for trees, robust for neural)\n   141вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ pipeline.py            # Combines all feature sets\n   142вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ regime/\n   143вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ detector.py            # Hierarchical regime detection\n   144вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ hmm.py                 # 2-state GaussianHMM\n   145вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ bocpd.py               # Bayesian Online Change Point Detection\n   146вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ garch.py               # GJR-GARCH(1,1)-t conditional volatility\n   147вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ efficiency_ratio.py    # Kaufman Efficiency Ratio\n   148вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ models/\n   149вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ lgbm_direction.py      # LightGBM ternary classifier\n   150вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ catboost_direction.py  # CatBoost ternary classifier\n   151вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gru_features.py        # GRU hidden state extractor\n   152вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ quantile.py            # LightGBM quantile regression (5 quantiles)\n   153вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ stacking.py            # Logistic regression meta-learner\n   154вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ calibration.py         # Isotonic regression calibration\n   155вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ tuning.py              # Optuna hyperparameter optimization\n   156вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ confidence/\n   157вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ meta_labeling.py       # Meta-labeling gate\n   158вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ conformal.py           # Conformal prediction gate\n   159вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ gating.py              # Full confidence gating pipeline\n   160вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ position_sizing.py     # Quarter-Kelly sizing\n   161вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ backtest/\n   162вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ walk_forward.py        # Purged walk-forward with embargo\n   163вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ engine.py              # Event-driven backtest engine (Numba)\n   164вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ cost_engine.py         # Transaction cost modeling (EXISTS)\n   165вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ metrics.py             # Sharpe, drawdown, profit factor, etc.\n   166вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ simulator.py           # Execution simulator with slippage\n   167вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ benchmarks/               # ALREADY EXISTS with code\n   168вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ __init__.py\n   169вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ data.py\n   170вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ engine.py\n   171вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ metrics.py\n   172вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ statistics.py\n   173вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ strategies.py\n   174вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ risk/                      # SPRINT 9 вҖ” Capital preservation (before backtesting!)\n   175вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ position_tracker.py    # Position state, mark-to-market, margin\n   176вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ kill_switches.py       # Daily/weekly/drawdown/consecutive loss halts\n   177вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ drawdown_gate.py       # Progressive position reduction (3%вҶ’15%)\n   178вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ volatility_guard.py    # Min/max vol filters, trading hours\n   179вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ position_sizer.py      # Quarter-Kelly, ATR stop, max hold period\n   180вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ risk_manager.py        # Orchestrates all risk components\n   181вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ events/\n   182вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ macro.py               # Event-driven macro module (CPI/FOMC)\n   183вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ cascade.py             # Liquidation cascade detector (Hawkes)\n   184вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”ңв”Җв”Җ monitoring/\n   185вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ alpha_decay.py         # CUSUM, rolling Sharpe, ADWIN\n   186вҶ’в”Ӯ       в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ drift.py               # Feature drift detection (PSI)\n   187вҶ’в”Ӯ       в””в”Җв”Җ api/\n   188вҶ’в”Ӯ           в””в”Җв”Җ server.py              # FastAPI endpoints\n   189вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ scripts/\n   190вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ collect_history.py             # Backfill historical data\n   191вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ train.py                       # Full training pipeline\n   192вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ backtest.py                    # Run backtests\n   193вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ live.py                        # Live prediction loop\n   194вҶ’в”ңв”Җв”Җ tests/\n   195вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_features/                 # Feature computation tests\n   196вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_models/                   # Model training/inference tests\n   197вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_ingest/                   # Data collection tests\n   198вҶ’в”Ӯ   в”ңв”Җв”Җ test_backtest/                 # Backtesting validation tests\n   199вҶ’в”Ӯ   в””в”Җв”Җ test_confidence/               # Gating pipeline tests\n   200вҶ’в””в”Җв”Җ docker/\n   201вҶ’    в”ңв”Җв”Җ Dockerfile\n   202вҶ’    в””в”Җв”Җ docker-compose.yml\n   203вҶ’```\n   204вҶ’\n   205вҶ’## How to Run\n   206вҶ’\n   207вҶ’### Setup\n   208вҶ’```bash\n   209вҶ’# Install dependencies\n   210вҶ’uv sync --all-extras\n   211вҶ’\n   212вҶ’# Verify installation\n   213вҶ’uv run python -c \"import ep2_crypto\"\n   214вҶ’```\n   215вҶ’\n   216вҶ’### Tests\n   217вҶ’```bash\n   218вҶ’# Run all tests\n   219вҶ’uv run pytest\n   220вҶ’\n   221вҶ’# Run with coverage\n   222вҶ’uv run pytest --cov=ep2_crypto --cov-report=term-missing\n   223вҶ’\n   224вҶ’# Run specific test module\n   225вҶ’uv run pytest tests/test_features/\n   226вҶ’```\n   227вҶ’\n   228вҶ’### Linting and Type Checking\n   229вҶ’```bash\n   230вҶ’# Lint\n   231вҶ’uv run ruff check src/ tests/\n   232вҶ’\n   233вҶ’# Format\n   234вҶ’uv run ruff format src/ tests/\n   235вҶ’\n   236вҶ’# Type check\n   237вҶ’uv run mypy src/ep2_crypto/\n   238вҶ’```\n   239вҶ’\n   240вҶ’### Data Collection\n   241вҶ’```bash\n   242вҶ’# Backfill historical data (60 days OHLCV, OI, funding)\n   243вҶ’uv run python scripts/collect_history.py\n   244вҶ’\n   245вҶ’# Start live data collection\n   246вҶ’uv run python scripts/live.py --collect-only\n   247вҶ’```\n   248вҶ’\n   249вҶ’### Training\n   250вҶ’```bash\n   251вҶ’# Full training pipeline (walk-forward)\n   252вҶ’uv run python scripts/train.py\n   253вҶ’\n   254вҶ’# Hyperparameter tuning\n   255вҶ’uv run python scripts/train.py --tune --trials 100\n   256вҶ’```\n   257вҶ’\n   258вҶ’### Backtesting\n   259вҶ’```bash\n   260вҶ’# Run full backtest with statistical validation\n   261вҶ’uv run python scripts/backtest.py\n   262вҶ’\n   263вҶ’# Run with specific date range\n   264вҶ’uv run python scripts/backtest.py --start 2025-01-01 --end 2025-03-01\n   265вҶ’```\n   266вҶ’\n   267вҶ’### API Server\n   268вҶ’```bash\n   269вҶ’# Start prediction API\n   270вҶ’uv run uvicorn ep2_crypto.api.server:app --host 0.0.0.0 --port 8000\n   271вҶ’```\n   272вҶ’\n   273вҶ’## Sprint Process\n   274вҶ’\n   275вҶ’Development follows 14 sprints defined in `SPRINTS.md`. Each sprint has:\n   276вҶ’- Clear objectives and deliverables\n   277вҶ’- Acceptance criteria that must pass before moving on\n   278вҶ’- Key files to create/modify\n   279вҶ’- Dependencies on previous sprints\n   280вҶ’\n   281вҶ’**Current sprint progress**: See `SPRINTS.md` for status.\n   282вҶ’\n   283вҶ’## Key Research References\n   284вҶ’\n   285вҶ’When implementing a module, consult the relevant research files in `research/`:\n   286вҶ’\n   287вҶ’| Module | Key Research Files |\n   288вҶ’|--------|-------------------|\n   289вҶ’| Microstructure features | `microstructure_ofi_microprice.md` |\n   290вҶ’| Meta-labeling | `meta_labeling_deep_research.md` |\n   291вҶ’| Monte Carlo validation | `monte_carlo_validation.md` |\n   292вҶ’| Stress testing | `STRESS_TESTING.md` |\n   293вҶ’| Transaction costs | `transaction_cost_modeling.md` |\n   294вҶ’| Model retraining | `retraining_strategies.md` |\n   295вҶ’| Statistical validation | `statistical_validation_tests.py` (executable code) |\n   296вҶ’| Full synthesis | `RESEARCH_SYNTHESIS.md` (root) |\n   297вҶ’| Backtesting methodology | `BACKTESTING_PLAN.md` (root) |\n   298вҶ’| Architecture decisions | `DECISIONS.md` (root) |\n   299вҶ’\n   300вҶ’## Risk Parameters (Starting Configuration)\n   301вҶ’\n   302вҶ’| Parameter | Value |\n   303вҶ’|-----------|-------|\n   304вҶ’| Position size per trade | 4-5% of capital (quarter-Kelly capped) |\n   305вҶ’| Daily loss limit | 2-3% of capital |\n   306вҶ’| Weekly loss limit | 5% of capital |\n   307вҶ’| Max drawdown halt | 15% of capital |\n   308вҶ’| Catastrophic stop per trade | 3 ATR |\n   309вҶ’| Max open positions | 1 |\n   310вҶ’| Max trades per day | 30 |\n   311вҶ’| Trading hours | 08:00-21:00 UTC (Europe + US sessions) |\n   312вҶ’| Weekend position sizing | -30% reduction |\n   313вҶ’| Confidence threshold | 0.60 (starting, adaptive) |\n   314вҶ’| Min bar volatility | 15% annualized |\n   315вҶ’| Max bar volatility | 150% annualized |\n   316вҶ’\n   317вҶ’## Critical Numbers\n   318вҶ’\n   319вҶ’| Parameter | Value |\n   320вҶ’|-----------|-------|\n   321вҶ’| Annualization factor | sqrt(105,120) = 324.22 (NOT sqrt(252)) |\n   322вҶ’| Bars per year | 288/day * 365 = 105,120 |\n   323вҶ’| Training window | 14 days (4,032 bars) sliding |\n   324вҶ’| Test window | 1 day (288 bars) |\n   325вҶ’| Purge size | 18 bars (90 min) |\n   326вҶ’| Embargo size | 12 bars (60 min) |\n   327вҶ’| Target backtest Sharpe | > 2.0 (to survive 50-70% degradation) |\n   328вҶ’| Break-even cost target | Strategy must survive > 15 bps round-trip |\n   329вҶ’| Expected live Sharpe | 0.6-1.0 (after degradation) |\n   330вҶ’| Round-trip cost assumption | 8-12 bps (conservative) |\n   331вҶ’\n   332вҶ’## Anti-Patterns to Avoid\n   333вҶ’\n   334вҶ’1. Never random-split time series data\n   335вҶ’2. Never use `bidirectional=True` on GRU (uses future data)\n   336вҶ’3. Never use centered rolling windows for features (look-ahead bias)\n   337вҶ’4. Never trust >70% directional accuracy without checking for look-ahead bias\n   338вҶ’5. Never use SMOTE or other oversampling on time series\n   339вҶ’6. Never interpolate missing data (forward-fill or drop only)\n   340вҶ’7. Never use global normalization (fit on all data) - always per-fold on training data\n   341вҶ’8. Never use expanding window for training - crypto non-stationarity makes old data harmful\n   342вҶ’9. Never skip transaction costs in backtest evaluation\n   343вҶ’10. Never commit without lint + typecheck + test passing\n   344вҶ’\n   345вҶ’## Research Reference\n   346вҶ’\n   347вҶ’All research is in `research/` with `research/INDEX.md` as the master lookup.\n   348вҶ’Files follow `RR-{category}-{topic}.md` naming. Key files per area:\n   349вҶ’\n   350вҶ’| Need to implement... | Read this first |\n   351вҶ’|---------------------|-----------------|\n   352вҶ’| WebSocket data ingestion | `RR-api-ccxt-exchange-integration.md` |\n   353вҶ’| Order book features (OBI, OFI) | `RR-ofi-microprice-implementation.md` |\n   354вҶ’| Liquidation cascade detection | `RR-cascade-liquidation-detection-system.md` |\n   355вҶ’| Cross-market NQ lead-lag | `RR-crossmarket-lead-lag-correlations.md` |\n   356вҶ’| Regime detection (HMM etc) | `RR-regime-detection-methods.md` |\n   357вҶ’| LightGBM training | `RR-lightgbm-crypto-tuning.md` |\n   358вҶ’| GRU/TCN architecture | `RR-gru-tcn-training-architecture.md` |\n   359вҶ’| Meta-labeling | `RR-metalabeling-implementation-guide.md` |\n   360вҶ’| Walk-forward validation | `RR-walkforward-validation-methods.md` |\n   361вҶ’| Backtesting framework | `RR-backtest-framework-design.md` |\n   362вҶ’| Statistical validation | `RR-stats-edge-vs-luck-tests.md` |\n   363вҶ’| Transaction costs | `RR-costs-transaction-cost-modeling.md` |\n   364вҶ’| Paper trading | `RR-papertrade-system-architecture.md` |\n   365вҶ’| Alpha decay monitoring | `RR-decay-edge-disappearance-detection.md` |\n   366вҶ’\n   367вҶ’## Pre-Code Checklists\n   368вҶ’\n   369вҶ’### Before writing ANY feature computation:\n   370вҶ’- [ ] Does it use ONLY data at times <= t? (no look-ahead)\n   371вҶ’- [ ] Is it tested with a truncation test?
